## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed the seed's distributed-execution paragraphs stand while the practice's own scale limits go unnamed, the package handles one fork at a time with three to five paths over horizons the user picks, it does not compose forks into decision trees, does not model adversarial responses beyond likely reactions, does not aggregate across a portfolio of simultaneous decisions, and its narrative method caps out where quantitative modeling begins
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the boundaries follow the format, narrative causal chains stay comprehensible at single-fork scale, branching them combinatorially or quantifying them exceeds what prose comparison can carry
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the characteristic overreach is the nested fork, simulating a decision whose timelines each contain further major decisions, the chains ballooning until no comparison table can hold them, the honest move being to simulate the near fork and name the far ones as inflection points
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: scale limits of the practice, corpus-execution splitting stays in the seed paragraphs
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the four boundaries, single-fork scope, non-adversarial reactions, no portfolio view, and the quantitative frontier
